<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9378545529833862974">They watched Danilo Silva for days before they finally grabbed him. He was living alone, a quiet life on a shady street in a small town in Brazil; a simple life in a modest home, certainly not one of luxury. Certainly no evidence of the fortune they thought he had stolen. He was much thinner and his face had been altered. He spoke a different language, and spoke it very we</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9378545529833862974">They watched Danilo Silva for days before they finally grabbed him. He was living alone, a quiet life on a shady street in a small town in Brazil; a simple life in a modest home, certainly not one of luxury. Certainly no evidence of the fortune they thought he had stolen. He was much thinner and his face had been altered. He spoke a different language, and spoke it very well.<br /><br />But Danilo had a past with many chapters. Four years earlier he had been Patrick Lanigan, a young partner in a prominent Biloxi law firm. He had a pretty wife, a new daughter, and a bright future. Then one cold winter night Patrick was trapped in a burning car and died a horrible death. When he was buried his casket held nothing more than ashes.<br /><br />From a short distance away, Patrick watched his own burial. Then he fled. Six weeks later, a fortune was stolen from his ex-law firm's offshore account. And Patrick fled some more. <br /><br />But they found him.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9378545529833862974">...more</a>

<div class="communityQuestion">
<div class="questionText">
<a href="/questions/456364-can-you-make-a-second-book-where-patrick">Can you make a second book where Patrick Lanigan finds Eva Miranda and has a reunion?</a>
</div>
<div class="communityQAFooter questionFooter">
<ul class="questionFooterActions">
<li class="footerItem like">
<span id="like_container_community_question_456364" class="likeItContainer"><a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F931362.The_Partner" class="jsLike like_it" rel="nofollow">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp">
<a href="/questions/456364-can-you-make-a-second-book-where-patrick">6 months ago</a>
</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionPermalink">
<a href="/questions/456364-can-you-make-a-second-book-where-patrick">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class="allCommunityAnswers">
<div class="communityAnswer">
<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/51119957-lenial-fitz" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/51119957-lenial-fitz">Lenial Fitz</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think that would be a great idea! She could find him because she misses him and realizes that she still loves him, but was temporarily blinded by<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think that would be a great idea! She could find him because she misses him and realizes that she still loves him, but was temporarily blinded by greed, which would be easy to do for any of us if tempted by that much money. Don'the judge. And of course, he instantly forgives her as he would want others to forgive him for his greed induced crimes.<br />I understand this would not make a very good novel, but maybe the bulk of the book could be about him searching for her and rebuilding his fortune. And her gradually losing her initial infatuation with the money, missing him, and finding him.<br />This, of course , would not be a Grisham novel, but a romance. But that's ok. Someone else could write it. I wonder if that would be allowed by copyright law?<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2823869">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12826202329774344130">I do own Grisham books, but only because family members keep buying them for me on birthday's and xmas's. I smile politely and thank them, wishing they would include the receipt. I have read this, and i don't recommend it unless you are 10 years old and want to start reading adult fiction. Dull, dull, dull. How this man is a best-selling writer is reflection of today's society's IQ.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="user" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?">Tadiana ? Night Owl?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=suspense" class="actionLinkLite">suspense</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=you-call-that-an-ending" class="actionLinkLite">you-call-that-an-ending</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=legal-eagles" class="actionLinkLite">legal-eagles</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1268243246">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14941324164060730758">A man jogging down a lonely road in Brazil is kidnapped and tortured, accused of being Patrick Lanigan, an American lawyer who was thought to have been killed in an automobile accident four years earlier--about the same time that $90 million disappeared from his law firm's offshore account. If he really is Lanigan, <strong>everyone</strong> wants a piece of him: his former partners, the client that the money came from, his wife, the insurance companies, the feds . . . Everyone. So is this guy really Patrick, and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14941324164060730758">A man jogging down a lonely road in Brazil is kidnapped and tortured, accused of being Patrick Lanigan, an American lawyer who was thought to have been killed in an automobile accident four years earlier--about the same time that $90 million disappeared from his law firm's offshore account. If he really is Lanigan, <strong>everyone</strong> wants a piece of him: his former partners, the client that the money came from, his wife, the insurance companies, the feds . . . Everyone. So is this guy really Patrick, and if so, what's his plan?<br /><br />I thought this was a highly entertaining legal thriller--implausible maybe, but who cares as long as it's fun?--until the very end. It lost a whole star with that ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[If you're going to pull off a twist like that, it needs some additional foundation. Foreshadowing. Something.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It felt like a cheap shot, manipulative and tacked-on, and left me more annoyed than an insurance company out a few million dollars. Or at least as annoyed as a reader out several hours and $26.50.<br /><br />My recommendation: rip the last few pages out of the book and pretend they were never there. Lalalala!<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9548252522154506415">Sometimes, John Grisham gives me 'forced' endings. Sometimes, I would imagine him going: <br />"When's the deadline again? I didn't expect the ending too and made me go "Oh." <br /><br />It is because of books like this Mr. Grisham (or would you prefer John?) that makes me want to pull your book out of anyone's bookshelf if I just want to pass the time. <br /><br />Now, would you be kind enough sir and tell me what happened? <br /> Was she kidnapped? <br /> Or simply ran away? <br /> I have think Stephano got her. <br /> Maybe this is her way of making Patrick pay. <br /><br />Am I suppose to loose sleep now?</span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer18010498880995771303">Brilliant strategizing, excellent suspense, but FRUSTRATING AND SAD ENDING.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />I love Grisham’s writing style. I was engaged all the way through. There was good action and a lot of suspense. By the end I was amazed, impressed, and intrigued with all the planning, strategizing, and how things worked out. It may not be believable but it was fun. Then the ending was frustrating and unhappy. I WANT HAPPY ENDINGS. Unfortunately that was my only problem with the book. I loved the experi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18010498880995771303">Brilliant strategizing, excellent suspense, but FRUSTRATING AND SAD ENDING.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />I love Grisham’s writing style. I was engaged all the way through. There was good action and a lot of suspense. By the end I was amazed, impressed, and intrigued with all the planning, strategizing, and how things worked out. It may not be believable but it was fun. Then the ending was frustrating and unhappy. I WANT HAPPY ENDINGS. Unfortunately that was my only problem with the book. I loved the experience. The only thing positive about the end was that it was thought provoking. I had to tell myself yes I could see that. But it’s not a story I want to hear. I normally would give this book a below average rating due to the ending, but because the rest was so good, I compromised at 3 stars. For someone who would enjoy smart-thinking, out-thinking others, and a good suspenseful read, go ahead.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />Patrick worked for a law firm that was about to receive 90 million dollars from a lawsuit, 60 million of which would go to their client Arecio. Patrick fakes his own death in a burning car. Soon after that, he steals the 90 million, transferring it to an offshore account. For four years he has been hiding with a fake name in Brazil. Arecio and two insurance companies hire Stephano to find Patrick. They have just found him. They kidnap and torture him asking “Where is the money?” Eva is a Brazilian lawyer who helps Patrick during this time.<br /><br />The narrator Frank Muller is great. He adds fun suspense and drama to his reading of the book.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Unabridged audiobook length: 11 hours 26 minutes. Narrator: Frank Muller. Swearing language: none that I recall. Sexual content: none. Setting: current day mostly various places in the U.S., plus S. America and Europe. Copyright: 1997. Genre: legal suspense.</span>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/369290-the-other-john?shelf=borrowed" class="actionLinkLite">borrowed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer30929511">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6826148281342993708">I'll give this one a grudging "check it out" rating. It's the tale of a lawyer, Patrick Lanigan, who had faked his death and then swiped ninety million dollars that his law firm had gathered in a settlement. As the book opens, it is four years later and Patrick is discovered. The rest of the book details how he attempts to escape the civil and criminal cases against him, intertwined with the details of how he pulled off the scam in the first place. Like the other Grisham novels I've read, the ch</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6826148281342993708">I'll give this one a grudging "check it out" rating. It's the tale of a lawyer, Patrick Lanigan, who had faked his death and then swiped ninety million dollars that his law firm had gathered in a settlement. As the book opens, it is four years later and Patrick is discovered. The rest of the book details how he attempts to escape the civil and criminal cases against him, intertwined with the details of how he pulled off the scam in the first place. Like the other Grisham novels I've read, the characters are well done. This is the first novel, though, where the hero of the tale is an honest-to-Ghandi bad guy. Well, mostly bad guy. Mr. Grisham does a good job of gaining sympathy for the character. Throughout the book, I found myself rooting for Patrick, feeling guilty all the while. Anyway, though it is an entertaining read, this has to be my least favorite of the Grisham novels I've read. While the caper is intricate, it's a bit too flawless. At the end, I have a hard time believing that it could really happen.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/2452767-marge" class="left imgcol" title="Marge"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1297826083p2/2452767.jpg" alt="Marge" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/126175827?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 13, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2452767-marge" class="user" title="Marge">Marge</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer126175827">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4907988647736584479">He had me at The Firm. Since then, I devoured every book of his. I would excitedly wait for a new book to come out and would be first in line to buy one. But for some reason, I missed this book. <br /><br />The protagonist is a disillusioned lawyer who went through some hoops to get himself seemingly entangled in a situation which as a reader I knew right away he would extract himself out of admirably. No surprise there. <br /><br />In a typical Grisham manner, the story is engaging, fast-paced, and clever. Not necessa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4907988647736584479">He had me at The Firm. Since then, I devoured every book of his. I would excitedly wait for a new book to come out and would be first in line to buy one. But for some reason, I missed this book. <br /><br />The protagonist is a disillusioned lawyer who went through some hoops to get himself seemingly entangled in a situation which as a reader I knew right away he would extract himself out of admirably. No surprise there. <br /><br />In a typical Grisham manner, the story is engaging, fast-paced, and clever. Not necessarily believable but one can easily forgive the liberties Grisham took to get the readers hooked. <br /><br />Although entertaining, it did not dazzle. I gave it 3 stars because the ending was contrived and predictable although I could tell that Grisham was going in for a shock of an ending. Sadly, I was not shocked. I was disappointed. There could have been a better ending. But what the heck, he still is a good storyteller.<br /><br />I would continue to buy (and read) his new books, one of which is coming out in Kindle edition a couple of weeks from now. Keep them coming, Mr. Grisham.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14301980035661842491">I finished reading this book within 3 days, a gripping story which full of twists and the unexpected. Here’s my 5 cent review...<br /><br />Luck was always on his side, his plans were well thought out, and they turned out to be perfectly schemed, and he finally succeed in buying his way out of jail, the punishment he always wanted to avoid, a nightmare to him.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText14301980035661842491">I finished reading this book within 3 days, a gripping story which full of twists and the unexpected. Here’s my 5 cent review...<br /><br />Luck was always on his side, his plans were well thought out, and they turned out to be perfectly schemed, and he finally succeed in buying his way out of jail, the punishment he always wanted to avoid, a nightmare to him. Started with how brilliantly he faked his death, ran away with his ex-firm’s USD 90 million and lived on the run for four years in Brazil, fell in love with and had a loyal companion in Eva, and finally when knowing that the people after him someday will be able to capture him, taught Eva meticulously how to vanish and what to do with the money and how to keep in touch with him when they had him in their custody. As the plots developed, Eva turned out to be a lovely wife-to-be, faithful friend, brilliant and dependable partner. But you have been warned, read until the last word...<br /><br />I feel something awkward about the ending. Never did it come across his mind even once that it would happen to him, that she would do that to him? True, that he had found his love in her, that they’d both had a wonderful feeling to each other, but how could he ruin his brilliant plans ever since he decided to part with his former life and begin a new one by putting so much undivided faith on her, and how could the shrewd master of scheming fell foolishly to his partner? Hemm, but that twisted ending certainly will give readers a great surprise, as it did to me...<br /><br /></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10185177699505275815">Patrick Lannigan, died in '92 in a car wreck and left behind, a wife and a daughter...<br />Or so everyone thought!<br />I practically drooled on every page of the novel, so gripped by the awesomeness <em>(that's the only word I can use)</em>, that is, Patrick Lannigan.<br />Now this guy! He fakes his death and disappears with 90 million dollars, then gets himself some hot Brazilian girlfriend. Is that a life or what?<br />I'm so tempted to give away all the spoilers, but out of the goodness of my heart, I'll let you all enjoy the rollercoaster joy of shifting through the mysteries.<br />Unfortunately, dear Pat gets caught <em>(then you get to the end of the novel and realize the truth)</em> by some sleazy thugs hired by the lovely lawyers who's money, Lannigan split with. They torture him to an inch from death but because Lannigan is awesome, he had everything planned out. His gf is notified he is missing by some wires tripped by the thugs and calls the FBI who then start looking for him.<br />After the FBI have him, another guy worthy of praise, Sandy gets introduced as an old friend of Pat now hired to be his lawyer.<br />The mysteries enthrall everyone. How did Pat pull of the theft? Who's body then was in the car wreck? What could Pat know that would have had him hunted so fiercely by these thugs? <em>(No, they weren't just after the money.)</em> How about this mysterious Brazillian woman? <em>(Who is a conniving witch by the way)</em><br />Definitely a great read! I'm such a fan of the characters, which in my opinion, Grisham drafted so well. I loved the whole Boston Legal, Private practice drama going on.<br />I'd recommend this book to anyone who loves a good thriller and a hell of a tasty plot.<br />P.S Lannigan is kinda the bad guy as well but his awesome</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_113217309">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113217309" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3901425-jerry" class="left imgcol" title="Jerry"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1412552940p2/3901425.jpg" alt="Jerry" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/113217309?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 24, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3901425-jerry" class="user" title="Jerry">Jerry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer113217309">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer120846279481011011"> "To Tell The Truth?"<br /><br />Quite a few years ago, there was a television show called "To Tell the Truth" in which a celebrity panel, egged on by a celebrity moderator, would try to guess which of three guest panelists, when quizzed about their lives and circumstances, would turn out to be the actual named person. The game always ended in the command "Will the real 'John Doe' please stand up", at which point our suspense was relieved and we all got to congratulate or commiserate on our own candidate of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText120846279481011011"> "To Tell The Truth?"<br /><br />Quite a few years ago, there was a television show called "To Tell the Truth" in which a celebrity panel, egged on by a celebrity moderator, would try to guess which of three guest panelists, when quizzed about their lives and circumstances, would turn out to be the actual named person. The game always ended in the command "Will the real 'John Doe' please stand up", at which point our suspense was relieved and we all got to congratulate or commiserate on our own candidate of choice.<br /><br />And so with our now famous author, sometimes we feel like saying "Will the real John Grisham please stand up." In Partner, this is not (to our minds, thankfully) the slow-paced dramatist of book one, A Time to Kill, or book five, The Chamber, the latter of which we predicted would never be a movie (wrong!) for its dullness and lack of intrigue (right!). Nor is this the social commentator proselytizing in The Rainmaker (wife abuse is bad) or The Runaway Jury (smoking is bad), although at least these two gave us moderately satisfying page-turners. Nope -- the good news is that our clever creator of Pelican Brief, The Client, and The Firm is back, with all the complexities of plot, action and thrills, even an ironic twist at the end, to captivate our imaginations and keep us up until three in the morning with no regrets. And make no mistake, a movie made from this novel will be a barn burner -- the only question being how many millions more will it dump into the Grisham coffers.<br /><br />By now, you may have heard snatches of the plot. We hate to spoil the story, but the gist is that a successful young law firm partner "dies" in an accident, only to be discovered years later hiding abroad with close to eight figures in stolen loot. [Relax -- all that becomes clear in chapter one of forty-three, so we're hardly giving away the plot...:] What follows are the intricacies of legal maneuvers and one-up-man-ship by our hero, as he masterminds his own extrication from prison, while gradually spinning the whole incredible yarn through various conversations meted out carefully enough to keep us turning pages into the wee hours.<br /><br />So, for us, the best John Grisham has indeed stood up -- with riveting story telling, political and social insight into the mechanisms of lawyering, and a tale that engrosses from start to finish. Can't wait for the movie ! <br /><br />{Reviewer's note -- no movie to date as far as we know...}</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="120846279481011011">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_274533811">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274533811" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7674967-oklahomadave" class="left imgcol" title="Oklahomadave"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Oklahomadave" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/274533811?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7674967-oklahomadave" class="user" title="Oklahomadave">Oklahomadave</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer274533811">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15787508583883132857">John Grisham has a curious way of drawing out courtroom fact, dramatic fiction, and credible dialog among compelling characters into entertaining legal page-turners. Unfortunately, Grisham's 1997 "The Partner" pulls together these elements among an only marginally interesting core of characters, all revolving around the capture and peculiar justice visited upon a presumed-dead partner in a Biloxi, Mississippi law firm.<br /><br />"The Partner" focuses on Patrick Lanigan, an attorney who fakes his own death,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15787508583883132857">John Grisham has a curious way of drawing out courtroom fact, dramatic fiction, and credible dialog among compelling characters into entertaining legal page-turners. Unfortunately, Grisham's 1997 "The Partner" pulls together these elements among an only marginally interesting core of characters, all revolving around the capture and peculiar justice visited upon a presumed-dead partner in a Biloxi, Mississippi law firm.<br /><br />"The Partner" focuses on Patrick Lanigan, an attorney who fakes his own death, heists $90 million from his law firm, and skips the country. After four years on the run, he's caught, and returned to the States presumably to face the consequences for his actions, yet he returns too prepared. Grisham works hard to make Lanigan into a sympathetic character, but the result leaves the reader among a bevy of characters that range from the irrelevant to the downright unpleasant, woven together by a narrative that slides too often into the tedious. One could almost argue that Grisham, amid writing "The Partner," realized Lanigan's one-dimensional, only marginally likable nature, and supplanted the novel with other, more sympathetic characters to compensate. <br /><br />As the novel's central character, Lanigan is the one on whom the entire story pivots. We must find a reason to care about what happens to him, yet the plot reveals a so thoroughly calculated character that we discover little of what happens to be much of a surprise. As a result, the character study becomes secondary to an exposition of the mechanics of a grand scam, with the drama and conflict virtually non-existent. The rest of "The Partner" borders on filler; attorneys talking to attorneys, investigators probing suspects, with seemingly every character holding a limitless supply of "secret files" on everyone else. While the material fills in the necessary blanks, the reader realizes there was no moral epiphany, no shocking surprise, no resonating arc that allows the "blanks" to make sense. Blanks, to be sure, are filled - but that's all. <br /><br />Contrasted against stories with much more richly drawn characters, such as Grisham's classic "The Firm," "The Partner" leaves the reader barely interested in how its main character acts. Most of Lanigan's life decisions are viewed only in retrospect, his conflicts viewed in the narrative as having been resolved outside the timespan of the novel's reality. We see only end-game. A more compelling version of "The Partner" could have been written in a story chronicling the meticulous planning of his original disappearance, and the detail behind the motivations that drove it. In a way, "The Partner" is a story about a novel not written.<br /><br />Those who have read "The Partner" surely know its final page twist that presumably serves as the ultimate ironic end game for Lanigan's character. We won't go into that ending here, but it is safe to say that very ending is so departed from the way Grisham has drawn the particular characters involved that the shock of the twist is quickly offset by the realization of its own absurdity. <br /><br />"The Partner" isn't a wholly bad Grisham novel; it contains the requisite complex plotting and the attention to legal details that pay homage to his tradition in the genre. The disappointment comes in the realization that, once the final page is turned, the drama, tension, and intrigue that have made his prior works so compelling are simply non-existent. With its focus on a story told almost entirely in retrospect if not flashback, and its odd last-page twist, "The Partner" cannot help but be termed a disappointment.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15787508583883132857">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_450769794">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450769794" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11085771-joseph" class="left imgcol" title="Joseph"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1350429918p2/11085771.jpg" alt="Joseph" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/450769794?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11085771-joseph" class="user" title="Joseph">Joseph</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer450769794">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2899540381627114585">Disappointing book. It has the requisite guilty pleasure moments of bad guys getting their comeuppances and a smart main character bobbing and weaving his way around the system, but Grisham also makes an attempt at a morality play and this portion of the book never seems fully fleshed out. <br /><br />The fun and strength of the book comes from the detailed telling of Patrick Lanigan faking his death and stealing a large sum of money in one fell swoop. The telling is mostly done through Lanigan recounting h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2899540381627114585">Disappointing book. It has the requisite guilty pleasure moments of bad guys getting their comeuppances and a smart main character bobbing and weaving his way around the system, but Grisham also makes an attempt at a morality play and this portion of the book never seems fully fleshed out. <br /><br />The fun and strength of the book comes from the detailed telling of Patrick Lanigan faking his death and stealing a large sum of money in one fell swoop. The telling is mostly done through Lanigan recounting his exploits to friends and associates and this seems to dull the action and tension a bit, as it is limited to his point of view. Lanigan comes off as a bit too omniscient having taken everything into account from the get go and planning accordingly. Save for his incarceration and treatment at the beginning, he doesn't seem to go through any significant trials. <br /><br />The major shortcoming of the book stems from the supposed guilt that Lanigan should feel for his actions and the people he affected through those actions. It is brought up, nominally discussed, then stops short. There is a debate of whether the ends justify the means, but only peripherally. There are several characters who question the integrity of Lanigan's actions and its effect on the justice system, but none of them seem to pursue it with any vigor. It's as if they just let Lanigan be Lanigan; they are in awe of him to do or say anything substantive. The book tosses out its own version of karma and it is supposed to be ironic, but these karmic moments wrap themselves up a little too neatly and just comes off disappointing the reader; there is not enough balance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2899540381627114585">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer92224870">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15658698245749881893">The ending came as a surprise, but frankly, it was disappointing and silly. The whole book was leading to a fantastic triumph, but no, Grisham has to rain on his own, the protagonist's (and the reader's) parade by yanking the happy-ever-after out from under everything. Look, dude, you got where you are by following a tried-and-true, formulaic model for popular fiction. We don't pick up a Grisham novel looking for great literature, we pick up a Grisham novel because we want to be entertained by a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15658698245749881893">The ending came as a surprise, but frankly, it was disappointing and silly. The whole book was leading to a fantastic triumph, but no, Grisham has to rain on his own, the protagonist's (and the reader's) parade by yanking the happy-ever-after out from under everything. Look, dude, you got where you are by following a tried-and-true, formulaic model for popular fiction. We don't pick up a Grisham novel looking for great literature, we pick up a Grisham novel because we want to be entertained by a tried-and-true, formulaic yarn. This pathetic attempt at tragedy fell on its face an unsatisfying thud. So why am I giving this three stars? Because, up until the last page or two, it was a fun read. Typical Grisham. Leave the tragedy to Hemingway and Dostoevsky.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1211488632">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211488632" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22299961-c-s-boag" class="left imgcol" title="C.S. Boag"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445042616p2/22299961.jpg" alt="C.S. Boag" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1211488632?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22299961-c-s-boag" class="user" title="C.S. Boag">C.S. Boag</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22299961-c-s-boag?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1211488632">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17412513780780528086">I read this hot on the heels of Iris Murdock's "The Nice and the Good" and they're as different as fish and fowl. Murdock's an intellectual- uses big words and intriguing insight. Grisham on the other hand is a machine- and in this novel the plot runs like the engine of a Ferrari.<br />How good he is. From the opening words, "They found him in Ponta Pa..." to the end; "Surely, one day she would find him," the story ticks over without missing a beat. The partner disappears with $90 million, a goodly su</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17412513780780528086">I read this hot on the heels of Iris Murdock's "The Nice and the Good" and they're as different as fish and fowl. Murdock's an intellectual- uses big words and intriguing insight. Grisham on the other hand is a machine- and in this novel the plot runs like the engine of a Ferrari.<br />How good he is. From the opening words, "They found him in Ponta Pa..." to the end; "Surely, one day she would find him," the story ticks over without missing a beat. The partner disappears with $90 million, a goodly sum- after faking his death. Through a series of beautifully logical stages, he's found - but the money isn't. Thus the story develops.<br /> Unlike in Murdock's novel, you don't really give a toss about the characters. And by the end, you find yourself to have been singularly unmoved. But the writer's ability leaves you breathless. Grisham, there's his picture on the inside back cove, smart-looking, sassy, knowing-knows how to do it- through all the natural twists and turns of the plot, to the hinted at, but still unexpected denouement.<br />Raindrops in the hair it's not - reality is never present, But he keeps you reading by unassailable logic. Clever boy, but different by far from Murdock. For what he does- 5/5</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17412513780780528086">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8280022473993179339">Ok, I know... All of Grisham's stuff is alike and pap and not good enough for real readers. That may be true but I like the stuff. I wait until the paperback, but I grab it and read it and like it. The Partner is another good one. Attorney Patrick Lanigan disappeared four years ago with $90 million dollars. Everyone is looking for him and then he's found… </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17276977024461793450"><a title="The Partner by John Grisham" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5350.The_Partner"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="The Partner by John Grisham" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/books/1388235158s/5350.jpg" /></a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/721.John_Grisham"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="John Grisham" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1413390525p2/721.jpg" /></a><br /><br />I had read The Partner by John Grisham years ago and have just recently re-read. I believe I am more impressed today with the novel than 15 years ago when first published. The way Grisham is able to tell a story is, of course, entertaining, but Grisham’s descriptions of attorneys, their behaviors, and their egos are absolutely hilarious and spot-on! If you want some insight into how our justice system behaves look no further. Here is an entertaining story that will provide all the fun of a gre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17276977024461793450"><a title="The Partner by John Grisham" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5350.The_Partner">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="The Partner by John Grisham" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/books/1388235158s/5350.jpg" /></a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/721.John_Grisham">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="John Grisham" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1413390525p2/721.jpg" /></a><br /><br />I had read The Partner by John Grisham years ago and have just recently re-read. I believe I am more impressed today with the novel than 15 years ago when first published. The way Grisham is able to tell a story is, of course, entertaining, but Grisham’s descriptions of attorneys, their behaviors, and their egos are absolutely hilarious and spot-on! If you want some insight into how our justice system behaves look no further. Here is an entertaining story that will provide all the fun of a great storyteller and the insight to the mechanics of a justice system fraught with egos, ineptitude and downhome stupidity. Enjoy!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer1201337044'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1201337044">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9348311424303912258">Really enjoyed this book, but hated the twist. I didn't believe the u-turn by a major character, to whose thoughts we'd been given access throughout the book. Also what she did doesn't make any sense: she could have easily split the money with him and still been rich without condemning herself to a lifetime on the run. I'd believe this far more if it was hinted that she had conspired with Stephano in order to grab a bigger share of the loot. But there was no evidence of that. I suspect the autho</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9348311424303912258">Really enjoyed this book, but hated the twist. I didn't believe the u-turn by a major character, to whose thoughts we'd been given access throughout the book. Also what she did doesn't make any sense: she could have easily split the money with him and still been rich without condemning herself to a lifetime on the run. I'd believe this far more if it was hinted that she had conspired with Stephano in order to grab a bigger share of the loot. But there was no evidence of that. I suspect the author threw this twist in late in the day to spice things up, but it spoiled the story for me, which ended on a sour note. Still love the writing though, and despite this misstep I liked the book overall.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1276115000">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6310057892516944671">More like 3.75 stars<br /><br />This is my 4th John Grisham book. I enjoy reading his novels very much. There is a certain simplicity and flow in his writing that makes them hard to put down. The concept in this book is interesting (though a little far fetched)and the ending is very good.<br /><br />Like all Grisham novels Ive read (so far) it always ends with me wanting more. Whether that be more story, more court-room drama or more action. He takes a great idea and weaves a quick and compelling story with such ease t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6310057892516944671">More like 3.75 stars<br /><br />This is my 4th John Grisham book. I enjoy reading his novels very much. There is a certain simplicity and flow in his writing that makes them hard to put down. The concept in this book is interesting (though a little far fetched)and the ending is very good.<br /><br />Like all Grisham novels Ive read (so far) it always ends with me wanting more. Whether that be more story, more court-room drama or more action. He takes a great idea and weaves a quick and compelling story with such ease that it is good but I wish it was more engaging? I compare it to Connelly who is such an expert at sucking you into the bleak world of LA that you become anxious to escape back to your safe reality.<br /><br />Despite this, I read the book quickly, enjoyed it, and plan on reading all the rest of his books too.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer192742526">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14607513284604056634">A good John Grisham book, but it just felt a little forced over his earlier novels.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_365868041">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365868041" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1384536-bigsna" class="left imgcol" title="Bigsna"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1298189411p2/1384536.jpg" alt="Bigsna" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/365868041?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1384536-bigsna" class="user" title="Bigsna">Bigsna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer365868041">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4176528668784021662">Read a John Grisham after a long long time - dont remember which was the last one i read. <br /><br />Strangely, while I was reading this book - I kept thinking of or more like missing the Millenium series novels. <br />Maybe it was because I was reading a suspense / thriller / on the run sort of book after a long time OR maybe I just missed the refined writing that those books had to offer. <br />From plot to detail to storyline. <br /><br />But, like I was discussing with a friend of mine who pointed out and rightly so, that the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4176528668784021662">Read a John Grisham after a long long time - dont remember which was the last one i read. <br /><br />Strangely, while I was reading this book - I kept thinking of or more like missing the Millenium series novels. <br />Maybe it was because I was reading a suspense / thriller / on the run sort of book after a long time OR maybe I just missed the refined writing that those books had to offer. <br />From plot to detail to storyline. <br /><br />But, like I was discussing with a friend of mine who pointed out and rightly so, that these two books/authors are incomparable - because the models they work on are completely different.<br /><br />While Larsson worked on his novels for a long time before putting them out there, Grisham churns one out every year! Maybe even sooner sometimes - which I realise greatly affects the quality of the writing. Both authors manage to make their books fast paced reads - edge of the seat, plot unravelling as you go - but its the relationship the reader develops with the characters that makes for an unforgettable book as against a forgettable one - like this one. :)<br /><br />Not that I am out to critically compare Grisham against Larsson but since the thought occured while reading this book - I thought I would mention it and see what others thought about it. <br /><br />Anyhow, coming to the book and its story - there were times when I wished that the detail would have been edited to a certain degree to make the story crisper, however the book still manages to keep you glued in until you've read it through. <br />I was happy that the book at least ended as I was hoping it would with a final twist in the master scheme - else it would have been too run of the mill usual.<br /><br />Good book to take a break from any heavy reading but would help to not have as many plots as it did - you kinda get lost in them and just want to move on to the next thing. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4176528668784021662">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_230566262">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230566262" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/738764-roderick-hart" class="left imgcol" title="Roderick Hart"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442961047p2/738764.jpg" alt="Roderick Hart" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/230566262?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/738764-roderick-hart" class="user" title="Roderick Hart">Roderick Hart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5350.The_Partner" title="Paperback 9780385339100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer230566262">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10206027932701801803">The partner in question is a lawyer, Patrick S Lanigan, who has stolen a large sum of stolen money from a bent client of his own bent law firm. Having done this, he has staged his own death and assumed a new identity in Brazil. This has the further advantage of getting him away from his wife who, apart from her body, leaves everything else to be desired.<br /><br />In Brazil he is finally tracked down by people working for those he had defrauded. Even under extreme torture he does not reveal where the money</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10206027932701801803">The partner in question is a lawyer, Patrick S Lanigan, who has stolen a large sum of stolen money from a bent client of his own bent law firm. Having done this, he has staged his own death and assumed a new identity in Brazil. This has the further advantage of getting him away from his wife who, apart from her body, leaves everything else to be desired.<br /><br />In Brazil he is finally tracked down by people working for those he had defrauded. Even under extreme torture he does not reveal where the money is. He can’t, since he has left it to his new Brazilian partner Eva, also a lawyer, to stash it away in safe places. <br /><br />The FBI get wind of what is happening just in time to extricate him from his tormentors and extradite him back to the US. At this point things get very legal indeed. To every new charge Patrick has a new solution. For me, reading all this legal stuff is about as interesting as watching paint dry or trying to follow a lengthy card game in a film. It’s all very clever and, as far as I can tell, very well done. But was it worth doing in the first place?<br /><br />Throughout the book there is evidence that Patrick buys his own publicity. He has an answer for everything and he knows it. So, given his hubris, we expect him to fall at the last hurdle. Which he does. So far, so predictable. The trouble is that the person who shafts him doesn’t give the slightest indication of such a mentality in previous chapters, quite the opposite. So the end is unconvincing.<br /><br />The book is ingenious, intricate, well put together and stocked with mostly intelligent but unsympathetic characters.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10206027932701801803">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe" class="user" title="Kaethe">Kaethe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer991022610">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5911911655452811237">"Poor John Grisham. He pretty much single-handedly creates a genre, achieves blockbuster status with only his second novel, and every further effort flies off the bookstore shelves and onto the movie screen. And then, when he writes yet another of his books, everyone bashes him for being boring.^M ^M <br /> Like The Firm, this is a novel about a man who is preternaturaly clever at figuring out the details. The protagonist is the same, although the name has been changed. I imagine this is Grisham's res</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5911911655452811237">"Poor John Grisham. He pretty much single-handedly creates a genre, achieves blockbuster status with only his second novel, and every further effort flies off the bookstore shelves and onto the movie screen. And then, when he writes yet another of his books, everyone bashes him for being boring.^M ^M <br /> Like The Firm, this is a novel about a man who is preternaturaly clever at figuring out the details. The protagonist is the same, although the name has been changed. I imagine this is Grisham's response to all those people who must have asked: ""But didn't they come looking?"" There are no surprises if you've read Grisham's other books, and plenty if you haven't. The most distinguishing factor for this book is a strong moral sensibility that hasn't been expressed since A Time To Kill. It isn't art, but it is fast-paced and cleverly plotted, which is why you pick up a Grisham after all."<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8557831698024913416">I enjoyed the story and finding out how it all worked out. It's sorta different from the other Grisham novels in that the hero isn't really a hero. He's a bad guy from the beginning but you still end up rooting for him against the other bad guys. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br />****Spoiler****<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I wasn't too surprised by one revelation at the end of him snitching on himself.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText8557831698024913416">I enjoyed the story and finding out how it all worked out. It's sorta different from the other Grisham novels in that the hero isn't really a hero. He's a bad guy from the beginning but you still end up rooting for him against the other bad guys. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br />****Spoiler****<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I wasn't too surprised by one revelation at the end of him snitching on himself. The surprise at the very end did get me as I still can't get where it came from. Totally out of the blue and sorta doesn't make sense. Maybe Patrick had to get his just desserts. If he walked off into the sunset with millions and the girl then it wouldn't be right with all the crap he put others through, including her. The story was 3rd person omniscient, but there didn't seem to be any indication from Eva that she felt any different about him and that she might bolt, no foreshadowing. It was just out of the blue and it sorta nags at me.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kz3/nMQQVBL0jsg845rXJeXdC2w3RU0veuxxHYvENPf26cBPNsJA6HhWvIed+zGXrCrIdX6YCoUQ5XSPR1HCsg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7TRs4I1n7FxjtxmW7jYdkuTaB5smhvLV4J2Qefn02gOI4FMzf7X4pu9vbS2QV/sgrS3Egm9btX+KlJXrNWEsRg==')})
  }

Their assassins then deliver a shocking ultimatum to the American government: set aside partisan politics and restore power to the people. No one, they warn, is out of their reach --- not even the president.\n\nA joint FBI-CIA task force reveals the killers are elite military commandos, but no one knows exactly who they are or when they will strike next. Only Michael O\'Rourke, a former U.S. Marine and freshman congressman, holds a clue to the violence: a haunting incident in his own past with explosive implications for his country\'s future     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/721.John_Grisham">About John Grisham</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/721.John_Grisham"><img alt="721" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1413390525p2/721.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16316359447493544379">"Long before his name became synonymous with the modern legal thriller, he was working 60-70 hours a week at a small Southaven, Mississippi law practice, squeezing in time before going to the office and during courtroom recesses to work on his hobby—writing his first novel.<br /><br />Born on February 8, 1955 in Jonesboro, Arkansas, to a construction worker and a homemaker, John Grisham as a child dreamed of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16316359447493544379">"Long before his name became synonymous with the modern legal thriller, he was working 60-70 hours a week at a small Southaven, Mississippi law practice, squeezing in time before going to the office and during courtroom recesses to work on his hobby—writing his first novel.<br /><br />Born on February 8, 1955 in Jonesboro, Arkansas, to a construction worker and a homemaker, John Grisham as a child dreamed of being a professional baseball player. Realizing he didn't have the right stuff for a pro career, he shifted gears and majored in accounting at Mississippi State University. After graduating from law school at Ole Miss in 1981, he went on to practice law for nearly a decade in Southaven, specializing in criminal defense and personal injury litigation. In 1983, he was elected to the state House of Representatives and served until 1990.<br /><br />One day at the DeSoto County courthouse, Grisham overheard the harrowing testimony of a twelve-year-old rape victim and was inspired to start a novel exploring what would have happened if the girl's father had murdered her assailants. Getting up at 5 a.m. every day to get in several hours of writing time before heading off to work, Grisham spent three years on A Time to Kill and finished it in 1987. Initially rejected by many publishers, it was eventually bought by Wynwood Press, who gave it a modest 5,000 copy printing and published it in June 1988.<br /><br />That might have put an end to Grisham's hobby. However, he had already begun his next book, and it would quickly turn that hobby into a new full-time career—and spark one of publishing's greatest success stories. The day after Grisham completed A Time to Kill, he began work on another novel, the story of a hotshot young attorney lured to an apparently perfect law firm that was not what it appeared. When he sold the film rights to The Firm to Paramount Pictures for $600,000, Grisham suddenly became a hot property among publishers, and book rights were bought by Doubleday. Spending 47 weeks on The New York Times bestseller list, The Firm became the bestselling novel of 1991.<br /><br />The successes of The Pelican Brief, which hit number one on the New York Times bestseller list, and The Client, which debuted at number one, confirmed Grisham's reputation as the master of the legal thriller. Grisham's success even renewed interest in A Time to Kill, which was republished in hardcover by Doubleday and then in paperback by Dell. This time around, it was a bestseller.<br /><br />Since first publishing A Time to Kill in 1988, Grisham has written one novel a year (his other books are The Firm, The Pelican Brief, The Client, The Chamber, The Rainmaker, The Runaway Jury, The Partner, The Street Lawyer, The Testament, The Brethren, A Painted House, Skipping Christmas, The Summons, The King of Torts, Bleachers, The Last Juror, and The Broker) and all of them have become international bestsellers. There are currently over 225 million John Grisham books in print worldwide, which have been translated into 29 languages. Nine of his novels have been turned into films (The Firm, The Pelican Brief, The Client, A Time to Kill, The Rainmaker, The Chamber, A Painted House, The Runaway Jury, and Skipping Christmas), as was an original screenplay, The Gingerbread Man. The Innocent Man (October 2006) marks his first foray into non-fiction.<br /><br />Grisham lives with his wife Renee and their two children Ty and Shea. The family splits their time between their Victorian home on a farm in Mississippi and a plantation near Charlottesville, VA.<br /><br />Grisham took time off from writing for several months in 1996 to return, after a five-year hiatus, to the courtroom. He was honoring a commitment made before he had retired from the law to become a full-time writer: representing the family of a railroad brakeman killed when he was pinned between two cars. Preparing his case with the same passion and dedication as his books' protagonists, Grisham successfully argued his clients' case, earning them a jur</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16316359447493544379">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/721.John_Grisham" class="actionLink moreLink">More about John Grisham...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
